  20. I was given the Wen kit as a gift by my mom who raved about it. I have to say, I was very skeptical at first because #1 it's an informercial, #2 some negative reviews I read, and #3 my mom and I have totally different hair (hers: fine, straight, dry, shoulder length, processed. mine: thick, wavy, long, oily at scalp but dry on ends, not heavily processed - only highlighted now and then). But I tried it anyway. After the first time, I thought eh, it's o.k. but I don't see the big deal. But I used it a few more times anyway. After the 3rd usage, I started to see a very noticable differenc in shine, softness and overall health. Now, after about 2 months of using Wen (with some trial and error) I have to say that I'm a total convert! I LOVE IT SO MUCH that I have thrown out my old shampoos and conditioners. For those thinking about trying it, DO IT. But, I have to say that there are some things that no one told me that I had to learn on my own:<br /><br />1. Did you read those negative reviews about Wen leaving their hair greasy? Me too. And it made me nervous. I did have a day in the beginning where my crown seemed a tiny bit greasy (as if I hadn't washed it in a few days). Here's what I learned that made all the difference. Do not try to put it on quickly and haphazardly like regular shampoo. You really have to work it in, and you really have to wash it out. I start out initially with a few pumps on concentrate solely on getting product into my roots (especially crown), around my hairline and at the nape of my neck. I really massage it in there making sure it's all the way to the roots and no hair is left uncoated. Only then to I move on to working it in to the length down the hair shaft and to the ends. I really feel like the Wen comb (or a good wide tooth comb) is essential. And then I leave it on through out the rest of my shower. Rinsing it out is the last thing I do. BE SURE to work on the rinse out as much as you did on the work in. Once again, make sure it's rinsed out of the crown and roots.<br /><br />2. The different scents are not just about smell. Go to Chaz Dean's site. They explain what type of hair each scent is meant to treat. I have tried Sweet Almond Mint, Pomegranate, Lavender, and Fig. Pomegranate is my favorite by far. Just moisturizing enough without loss of body.<br /><br />I went from being a total skeptic to a complete kool-aid drinking convert. I hope this review has left you with some tips that I had to discover on my own.

Neither happened.<br /><br />That evening my hair looked just as clean as when it was first washed and the little bit of frizz I did have was nothing compared to my normal frizz factor. After all, I live outside of Miami Florida, the hair frizz capital of the world. Normally my hair will stay down until maybe lunch time, on a good day, before it's so out of control from frizz, I give up and put it into a bun or ponytail. Amazingly, with the Wen I kept it down all day.<br /><br />The next morning my scalp was oily but not more than normal. Again I used the Wen Sweet Almond Conditioner but followed it up with my own styling products. Again, I had a good hair day.<br /><br />Now the big test was coming up. I've been in need of hair color and highlights and went in two weeks ago. Normally coloring and highlighting my hair results in straw that I will have to deep condition for days following a color just to get some softness back and to help tame my hair. I always wait two days after receiving color to wash my hair and on the second day I decided to try the Wen. If this product was really going to work, this was the ultimate test.<br /><br />I again followed the instructions and after washing my hair I followed it up with the re-moist mask, leaving it on for about an hour and rinsed very well. My hair did not feel like straw at all, the color had not faded one bit and once again, using my own straightening products, I was able to blow-dry my hair in about 1/2 the time and without battling as much frizz. Since coloring, I've been washing my hair every other day and using the re-moist mask once a week.<br /><br />I've now had two weeks to evaluate the product and have to admit I've gone from skeptical to very happy. I have found once a week I do needto use a regular shampoo just to remove some buildup on my scalp that Wen does seem to leave. I use Alterna Caviar or Alterna-10 shampoo for that, also a non-sulfate shampoo and follow that up with the Wen Mask.<br /><br />I will be purchasing more of the Conditioning Shampoo and Wen re-moist mask. I do wish Wen would devise a Conditioning Shampoo that would work better for those of us with oily hair but using normal shampoo from time to time isn't that big of a deal.<br /><br />I would definitely recommend Wen for those with curly, frizzy hair as it does seem to do wonders.<br /><br />I've rated the Wen kit 4 stars, while I really like the Conditioner, the re-moist mask and the included comb, Wen's texture balm is worthless for me as is the styling cream.<br /><br />I hope this review helps.

When I opened my second bottle I put half the product in the empty bottle and mixed in about half a bottle of purified water. Shook it up for a while and it regained a thick texture. I used half the number of the diluted stuff on my hair, washed it out when I was finished as I would any other product (rather than using the longer time frames for both washing and rinsing suggested) and my hair turned out great. I have continued with this procedure since and the product is working well enough for me to continue using it.<br /><br />So here is some anecdotal information about \\"performance\\". I am not sure I would say that I see a huge difference between the outcome of my hair with this product vs. using shampoo and conditioner. My hair looks shiny and healthy, but when I have used other products because I was traveling or something, it also looked good. Some other products make my hair look thicker, however, I don't know if over time they would also make it look dryer. I haven't tested it because I am pretty happy with the Wen.<br /><br />That said, I WILL say this. About two years ago I decided to begin blending the increasing amount of grey hair on my head using more highlights. Obviously, to get them to blend with the grey they were quit light, using a lot of that nasty peroxide that can really take a toll on your hair. My hairdresser was so worried my fine, thin hair would not hold up to this aggressive treatment. She started slowly and every time she was finished she stood stunned at how sturdy my hair was. When we finally got to the full treatment of highlights which would typically cause a lot of damage, she was just amazed at how healthy my hair continued to be. She thinks I have biotic hair, which was never the case in the past. My hair was prone to being dull and easily damaged.<br /><br />So for me, having a single product that is conveniently delivered to my door for less cost as the other products I had been using is a good thing. Knowing that my hair can withstand the harsh coloring treatments I get and still look healthy and shiny is a huge plus. Thus, the 4 star rating. I would have given it a 5 star, but its troubling to me that the instructions are so complicated and the recommended amounts such overkill. I even called the company and asked about the amounts (they say that the best results come from using a lot of product and leaving it on a long time, neither of which have proven true for me) and the CSR told me that others have found it to be true that they get better results with less product. This smells to me of a means of getting customers to use more product than they need so they can order more. I think thata business should have more integrity than that, and getting a customer like me who uses less but orders religiously should be good enough.<br /><br />Two other points in regard to other things posted in reviews. First, dealing with GR has been an unusually POSITIVE experience for me. Their CSR have been accommodating, tending to err to my favor, and refunds or adjustments were handled without any grief. In fact, some time back a very evil ex friend of mine had over 80 as-seen-on-tv items sent to my address, many coming from GR. They were very helpful in getting these charges off my credit cards and did not require me to return a single product. I have written a more detailed review about this which you can find if you look for all my reviews.<br /><br />Finally, about the cost. The original $39 a month was just too much for me to spend, even when diluting the product. I called and discussed this with them because I was going to cancel. They reduced my monthly shipment to $24 a month. I have found this to be the case for almost every company I have used for auto-ship. That is how the price is manageable for me; I tend to use less than two diluted bottles a month and get shipments every 4-5 months.

  238. First off, let me tell you that I am a person who is very skeptical about infomercial items. When it comes to items advertised on television I'm usually a pessimist. The few products I have bought from TV in the past turned out to be absolute duds. So needless to say; I'm not a big TV shopper, or a believer of infomercial items. However, after happening on the Wen infomercial while channel surfing; I was immediately pulled in because I have EXTREMELY fussy straight hair and no shampoo or hair product EVER works quite right for me. Shampoos like Suave or Dove dry out my hair to the point where it looks like straw, and leave in conditioners make my hair look like an oil slick. Even salon shampoos like the Paul Mitchell line make my hair look limp and lifeless. So yeah I admit, when I saw the Wen infomercial I was a bit skeptical, but being as I was so desperate for a product that would make my hair look halfway decent; I went ahead and took the risk... and oh wow am I happy I did! My husband kept laughing at me when I blow dried my hair out after the first time of using this product, because I kept shouting; \\"Oh my god! Wow!\\" from the bathroom. My hair has NEVER looked this healthy, clean, vibrant, or full of body. I got instant and visible results, just like in the infomercial. The product smells wonderful and it makes my usually dry hair so soft to the touch. I am so happy with this product and highly recommend it to others who have fussy hair and have also never been able to find the right product. For me, Wen is worth every penny! Two thumbs way up!<br /><br />Now, that all being said, bare in mind there are a few things to consider before buying/trying Wen:<br /><br />1.) Despite what the commercial says, like all things, it doesn't work for everyone. I have talked to a few other people that have used it, and just like all shampoos; it works for some and not others. I happen to be one of the hair types it works great on.<br /><br />2.) The longer and thicker yourhair is, the more this will cost you. The infomercial states that every supply is by month or two months, etc, but I have talked to a few girls with very long hair who have used it, and they say that their \\"monthly\\" supply was gone in just a few uses. I happen to have short hair so my supply actually lasts, but this won't be the case for people with long hair.<br /><br />3.) Be careful how much you use and unless you have long hair, do NOT use as much as directed on the back. My hair is chin length and 6-8 pumps works great from me. The back says to use 10-15 pumps, but if you use that much on short hair its a total waste of product.<br /><br />4.) If you have hair that's easily weighed down or easily becomes oily; avoid using the texture balm. All the other products that came in my Wen set worked great, expect for the balm. Just a tiny bit of it made my hair look chunky, oily, and weighed down, which pretty much counteracted the fabulous results I got from the Wen shampoo itself. I'm sure the texture balm would work great for people who have thicker hair, but for people who have baby fine hair like me, its not all that great.<br /><br />Just a few things to keep in mind. I really do hope the Wen system will work for you as well as it did for me.

  422. Hi Wen is not for everyone but it can be a great product but you really have to follow the instructions<br /><br />1) Each product is for a differnt hair type go to the Wen Website to find what is right for you. Fig is for thicker, curly or color treated hair, Sweet Almond Mint and Pomegrante are universal formulas, Tea Tree for Scalp issues, Lavender for fine hair provides volume, Cucumber Aloe fine hair that tends to have oily scalp and dry ends.<br /><br />2) You neeed to use the right amount of product for your hair length. My hair is fine and color treated a few inches below my shoulders. They say to apply in 4 sections your crown, underneath and back of head and each side. I use 8-9 pumps for each section. If I use less my hair does not come out as good. Comb it through with wide tooth comb this is important. Then clip it up and leave on 3-5 minutes<br /><br />3) the most important step rinse with as cold as water as you can stand and rinse really well. Warm water will not rinse it out totally.<br /><br />4) You can mix types also. For every day I use Cucumber Aloe followed above and after shower use 1-2 pump as leave in conditions on my ends. If I neeed extra mositure and/or volume or for weekend when I blow dry my hair I use Lavendar on crown and fig everywhere. This give me volume at crown and extra moisture on ends.<br /><br />When I air dry my air and its thicker, more volume and shiny. When I blow dry and add volumizing spray or mouse it's smooth with volume and thicker and shiny.<br /><br />They also sell another product which is you are supposed to use less of and it's suppossed to be even better called six Thirteen which I will be trying next.
